So sorry.<span class='line-break'> </span> Josie ironed a big pile of<span class='line-break'> </span> clothes today and raked on<span class='line-break'> </span> the yard some.<span class='line-break'> </span> I got dinner.  I churned.<span class='line-break'> </span> This evening I went to <span class='line-break'> </span> Marvins.  I guess they will<span class='line-break'> </span> call the baby Julia.  I am<span class='line-break'> </span> glad of it.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mabel has bin good today<span class='line-break'> </span> for her to be.  All of the rest<span class='line-break'> </span> of the children went to<span class='line-break'> </span> school.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1449">
<h3><a name="page-1449">Saturday November 19, 1921</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>Cloudy most of the day<span class='line-break'> </span> and some rain.  Very warm<span class='line-break'> </span> for Nov.  Ben &amp; Jim worked<span class='line-break'> </span> on tobacco some and sowed<span class='line-break'> </span> some wood.<span class='line-break'> </span> Josie got dinner.<span class='line-break'> </span> I have sewed on my quilt <span class='line-break'> </span> the most of the day.<span class='line-break'> </span> Finished tonight.  I am glad <span class='line-break'> </span> it is finished.<span class='line-break'> </span> I have bin at home all<span class='line-break'> </span> day.  I wanted to go to<span class='line-break'> </span> the river so bad this<span class='line-break'> </span> evening but no one would<span class='line-break'> </span> take me from here and<span class='line-break'> </span> I did not ask any one<span class='line-break'> </span> to take me.<span class='line-break'> </span> I work like a slave and<span class='line-break'> </span> then Ben dont take me<span class='line-break'> </span> any wher when he can<span class='line-break'> </span> reasonably get out of it.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1450">
<h3><a name="page-1450">Sunday November 20, 1921</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A cloudy day &amp; some rain.<span class='line-break'> </span> We all was at home until<span class='line-break'> </span> after dinner.  Josie and I got<span class='line-break'> </span> dinner.  I killed and dressed<span class='line-break'> </span> two chickens and fried them.<span class='line-break'> </span> Josie baked some pies.  I <span class='line-break'> </span> churned this evening.  Jim<span class='line-break'> </span> went to see John Hutchersons<span class='line-break'> </span> hogs.  Met up with Mr Jess[?]<span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; Willie Hutcherson and Will<span class='line-break'> </span> Alen and spent the evening<span class='line-break'> </span> walking and talking.  Henry<span class='line-break'> </span> B went to Dr Owens.  He<span class='line-break'> </span> rode Jake, Bens horse.  The [?]<span class='line-break'> </span> broke and Henry fell off.  It<span class='line-break'> </span> did not hurt him.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben &amp; Josie, Edna &amp; Franklin<span class='line-break'> </span> and Mabel and I went to<span class='line-break'> </span> Marvins.  They were all well.<span class='line-break'> </span> One of the turkeys is sick<span class='line-break'> </span> and I expect it will die.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1451">
<h3><a name="page-1451">Monday November 21, 1921</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A beautiful day.  Jim &amp; <span class='line-break'> </span> Ben shucked some corn this<span class='line-break'> </span> morning and fed the cows<span class='line-break'> </span> the stalks.  Then they stripped<span class='line-break'> </span> tobacco until dinner.  Josie<span class='line-break'> </span> and I persuaded Ben to go<span class='line-break'> </span> to the mill.  Josie shelled<span class='line-break'> </span> some corn whle washed<span class='line-break'> </span> the dishes.  We went with<span class='line-break'> </span> him.  We fished some.  We<span class='line-break'> </span> caught 39 fish dressed<span class='line-break'> </span> them and intend to cook them<span class='line-break'> </span> for breakfast in the morning.<span class='line-break'> </span> I was so glad to go fishing.<span class='line-break'> </span> We come by the store and<span class='line-break'> </span> bought a few things.<span class='line-break'> </span> Jim and Ben tied some<span class='line-break'> </span> tobacco to night.<span class='line-break'> </span> The children went to school<span class='line-break'> </span> except Mabel.  She went<span class='line-break'> </span> with us fishing.  I have not<span class='line-break'> </span> seen any of Marvins folks<span class='line-break'> </span> today.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1452">
<h3><a name="page-1452">Tuesday November 22, 1921</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A very good day.  Ben &amp; Jim<span class='line-break'> </span> stripped tobacco.  Josie helped<span class='line-break'> </span> to tie some this evening.<span class='line-break'> </span> Josie got dinner and scrubed<span class='line-break'> </span> the dining room floor.  Marvin<span class='line-break'> </span> moved two loads of hay to his <span class='line-break'> </span> home near Gretna.<span class='line-break'> </span> I went to Johnson Reynolds<span class='line-break'> </span> this evening.  Mollie was<span class='line-break'> </span> sewing.  Lizzie Bennett<span class='line-break'> </span> come here this evening<span class='line-break'> </span> and as I was not at home<span class='line-break'> </span> she come to Johnsons.  She eat<span class='line-break'> </span> supper there.  I thought I <span class='line-break'> </span> would stay until bed time<span class='line-break'> </span> but Ben come for me.  I <span class='line-break'> </span> was glad to ride home.<span class='line-break'> </span> Lizzie brought me two<span class='line-break'> </span> nice pumpkins.  I am so glad<span class='line-break'> </span> of them.  Mollie gave me<span class='line-break'> </span> some turnip greens.  I <span class='line-break'> </span> glad of that.  Hope to enjoy them.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1453">
<h3><a name="page-1453">Wednesday November 23, 1921</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Ben &amp; Jim<span class='line-break'> </span> stripped tobacco all day.  They<span class='line-break'> </span> finished a cureing.  Marvin<span class='line-break'> </span> went to Gretna hauling feed.<span class='line-break'> </span> Carrie and the little children<span class='line-break'> </span> come here.  It was the first<span class='line-break'> </span> time that the new baby<span class='line-break'> </span> was a way from home.  I hope it<span class='line-break'> </span> wont hurt her.  Hazel &amp; <span class='line-break'> </span> Eva was very good to day.<span class='line-break'> </span> Kate Harvey come this evening.<span class='line-break'> </span> I was glad for her to come.<span class='line-break'> </span> Was sorry for her to have<span class='line-break'> </span> to take such a long walk.<span class='line-break'> </span> Hope it wont hurt her.<span class='line-break'> </span> The children went to<span class='line-break'> </span> school to day.<span class='line-break'> </span> Alcie washed here to day.<span class='line-break'> </span> I have peiced one square<span class='line-break'> </span> for a quilt.<span class='line-break'> </span> 9:30 oclock</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1454">
<h3><a name="page-1454">Thursday November 24, 1921</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day and warm.  There was <span class='line-break'> </span> a rain bow was in the clouds<span class='line-break'> </span> this morning.  It has rained a little<span class='line-break'> </span> tonight.  Ben &amp; Jim shucked some<span class='line-break'> </span> corn.  Then they comence to cover<span class='line-break'> </span> the shed.  Riped off the shingles.<span class='line-break'> </span> Josie ironed some this morning.<span class='line-break'> </span> I churned &amp; killed a chicken.<span class='line-break'> </span> We cooked some parships the<span class='line-break'> </span> first time this fall.  Kate Harvey<span class='line-break'> </span> come and brought us some salit.<span class='line-break'> </span> Reese Smith carried me to White<span class='line-break'> </span> Falls.  I caught several fish.<span class='line-break'> </span> Paul Smith caught two fish.<span class='line-break'> </span> We come back by Renan store.<span class='line-break'> </span> Jim Thomson and family was<span class='line-break'> </span> there.  Four of Mag Brumfield<span class='line-break'> </span> children was at the store.<span class='line-break'> </span> They all looked well.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mr Meguary[?]was here<span class='line-break'> </span> this morning.  We bought<span class='line-break'> </span> a few things from him.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1455">
<h3><a name="page-1455">Friday November 25, 1921</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Some cooler.<span class='line-break'> </span> Jim &amp; Ben covered the<span class='line-break'> </span> shed to the stable.  Got it<span class='line-break'> </span> a bout done.  Marvin<span class='line-break'> </span> carried a load of feed to<span class='line-break'> </span> his new home.<span class='line-break'> </span> Josie got dinner.  I ironed<span class='line-break'> </span> some this evening.  Denia<span class='line-break'> </span> Blair come over a while.<span class='line-break'> </span> She has a bad colde.  I was<span class='line-break'> </span> glad that she come.  Lee<span class='line-break'> </span> Brumfield killed a beef.<span class='line-break'> </span> We got a peice of it and<span class='line-break'> </span> Carrie got some.  Reese went<span class='line-break'> </span> to Renan for it.  I am<span class='line-break'> </span> glad to get it.<span class='line-break'> </span> The children went to school<span class='line-break'> </span> today.  Sellie Blair gave<span class='line-break'> </span> Henry a mess of salit.<span class='line-break'> </span> He forgot and left it at<span class='line-break'> </span> the school house.</p>
</div>
</div>

<div id="page-1456">
<h3><a name="page-1456">Blank</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1457">
<h3><a name="page-1457">Sunday November 27, 1921</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A cloudy day and rain this<span class='line-break'> </span> evening.  We all staid at<span class='line-break'> </span> home until dinner.  It looked<span class='line-break'> </span> as if it was going to clear off.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben and family went to<span class='line-break'> </span> Mr Powers.  It rain a gain<span class='line-break'> </span> before they got there.  They<span class='line-break'> </span> made it home all right<span class='line-break'> </span> before dark.<span class='line-break'> </span> Jim and I went to Marvins.<span class='line-break'> </span> Jim and Marvin walked<span class='line-break'> </span> a round and got about<span class='line-break'> </span> wet.  Ben &amp; family<span class='line-break'> </span> and got home just before<span class='line-break'> </span> dark.  It is very warm<span class='line-break'> </span> for the time of year.<span class='line-break'> </span> Most evry one wants is to<span class='line-break'> </span> get colde so they can kill<span class='line-break'> </span> hogs.  Johnson Reynolds and<span class='line-break'> </span> John Hutcherson have their<span class='line-break'> </span> trucks loaded ready to start<span class='line-break'> </span> to Danvill in the morning.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1458">
<h3><a name="page-1458">Monday November 28, 1921</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>Cloudy most of the day.<span class='line-break'> </span> Jim dodged a bout all morning.<span class='line-break'> </span> In the evening Ben &amp; Josie<span class='line-break'> </span> went to Gretna.<span class='line-break'> </span> Jim worked on the cow stalls.<span class='line-break'> </span> Henry &amp; Edna went to school.<span class='line-break'> </span> I worked on my quilt<span class='line-break'> </span> about all day.<span class='line-break'> </span> Josie got dinner.<span class='line-break'> </span> The wind is blowing now.<span class='line-break'> </span> I think it is getting colde.<span class='line-break'> </span> I have read un til a late<span class='line-break'> </span> hour tonight.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1459">
<h3><a name="page-1459">Tuesday November 29, 1921</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A <a href='../subjects/9394' title='good'>good</a> day.  Ben and <a href='../subjects/141' title='Jim Brumfield'>Jim</a><span class='line-break'> </span> <a href='../subjects/298' title='corn shucking'>shucked some corn</a> and loaded<span class='line-break'> </span> <a href='../subjects/141' title='Jim Brumfield'>Jims</a> <a href='../subjects/454' title='tobacco'>tobacco</a> on <a href='../subjects/68' title='John Hutcherson'>John<span class='line-break'> </span> Hutcherson</a> <a href='../subjects/219' title='truck'>truck</a>.  John &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span> Jim started to <a href='../subjects/973' title='Danville, Virginia'>Danville</a>.<span class='line-break'> </span> I hope they got there<span class='line-break'> </span> ok.  This evening Ben <span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; <a href='../subjects/9366' title='Marvin'>Marvin</a> went to the<span class='line-break'> </span> <a href='../subjects/254' title='school'>school house</a> and helped to<span class='line-break'> </span> put a <a href='../subjects/7310' title='pump'>pump</a> in the <a href='../subjects/8224' title='well'>well</a><span class='line-break'> </span> that has bin bored there.<span class='line-break'> </span> They staid late.  The children<span class='line-break'> </span> come home with them.<span class='line-break'> </span> <a href='../subjects/8488' title='Josie'>Josie</a> had <a href='../subjects/71' title='supper'>supper</a> ready<span class='line-break'> </span> when they got home.<span class='line-break'> </span> I <a href='../subjects/10496' title='cutting pieces'>cut peices</a> and <a href='../subjects/29' title='sewing'>sewed</a><span class='line-break'> </span> on my <a href='../subjects/8' title='quilting'>quilt</a> most of<span class='line-break'> </span> the day.  Hope to finish<span class='line-break'> </span> the squares tomorrow if<span class='line-break'> </span> I work on it.  I wanted to<span class='line-break'> </span> go to <a href='../subjects/5' title='Marvin Smith'>Marvins</a> this evening but<span class='line-break'> </span> would not leave Josie <a href='../subjects/9204' title='Mabel'>Mabel</a>.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1460">
<h3><a name="page-1460">Wednesday November 30, 1921</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A beautiful day for Nov.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben put in some window glass<span class='line-break'> </span> this morning.  This evening<span class='line-break'> </span> they worked on the pump<span class='line-break'> </span> at the school house.  Did <span class='line-break'> </span> not get it fixed.  Jim did not<span class='line-break'> </span> come home tonight.  Denia<span class='line-break'> </span> and Cordie Blair come here<span class='line-break'> </span> this evening and then went <span class='line-break'> </span> to Mr Woodings.  I am sorry<span class='line-break'> </span> I was not at home.  I had<span class='line-break'> </span> ask Oscar Brumfield to take<span class='line-break'> </span> me fishing.  He carried<span class='line-break'> </span> his mother and I to the<span class='line-break'> </span> river at White Falls.  We<span class='line-break'> </span> caught 40 fish.  I was so<span class='line-break'> </span> glad to go.  I do love to go<span class='line-break'> </span> but when I get home and<span class='line-break'> </span> can see what a fool they think<span class='line-break'> </span> I am then I wish I had staid at home.<span class='line-break'> </span> I have finished twenty squares<span class='line-break'> </span> for Josies quilt.<span class='line-break'> </span> nine oclock at night</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1461">
<h3><a name="page-1461">Thursday December  1, 1921</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A beautiful day.  Ben hauled<span class='line-break'> </span> some lightwood this morning.  This<span class='line-break'> </span> evening he went to Strait Stone<span class='line-break'> </span> and brought Mr George Worsham<span class='line-break'> </span> up to the school house and<span class='line-break'> </span> carried him back.  They got<span class='line-break'> </span> the pump to work so they can<span class='line-break'> </span> get water at the school house.<span class='line-break'> </span> The picture agent come this <span class='line-break'> </span> evening and brought Josies<span class='line-break'> </span> pictures.  Carrie Smith had<span class='line-break'> </span> a lot of company this evening.<span class='line-break'> </span> Kate Harvey &amp; Mag Brumfield,<span class='line-break'> </span> Mollie Reynolds and Josie and<span class='line-break'> </span> Mabel.  Otho Blair and Sallie<span class='line-break'> </span> and I went fishing.  Did not<span class='line-break'> </span> catch many fish but had a<span class='line-break'> </span> pleasant evening.  I was so glad<span class='line-break'> </span> that they carried me.  Marvin<span class='line-break'> </span> has his waggon loaded to<span class='line-break'> </span> got to Gretna.  I fear it will<span class='line-break'> </span> rain by morning.  Jim has<span class='line-break'> </span> not come home yet.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1462">
<h3><a name="page-1462">Friday December  2, 1921</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>Rain this morning and this evening.<span class='line-break'> </span> Henry went to school.<span class='line-break'> </span> Marvin carried his children<span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; Henry.  Ben worked on<span class='line-break'> </span> Marvins car the most of the day.<span class='line-break'> </span> Jim come home to night.  Ben<span class='line-break'> </span> met him and brought him<span class='line-break'> </span> home.  Josie made me three<span class='line-break'> </span> aprons and got dinner.<span class='line-break'> </span> This evening she ironed <span class='line-break'> </span> some collars and six<span class='line-break'> </span> nice shirts.<span class='line-break'> </span> I ironed all the washing<span class='line-break'> </span> excep the shirts and collars.<span class='line-break'> </span> I went to Marvins.  Carrie<span class='line-break'> </span> was makeing Hazel a dress.<span class='line-break'> </span> Henry brought us a pound<span class='line-break'> </span> of butter from Otho Blairs<span class='line-break'> </span> to day.  Mabel is not<span class='line-break'> </span> well tonight.  I hope she<span class='line-break'> </span> may be well soon.<span class='line-break'> </span> Carrie talked with Ethel this evening.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1463">
<h3><a name="page-1463">Saturday December  3, 1921</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A beautiful day.  Ben &amp; <span class='line-break'> </span> Jim &amp; Henry sawed wood all<span class='line-break'> </span> day and did not get done.  Jim<span class='line-break'> </span> went to Hutchersons and got oil<span class='line-break'> </span> and Ben went to Renan and<span class='line-break'> </span> got oil.  Josie has had a time<span class='line-break'> </span> with Mabel.  She has bin sick<span class='line-break'> </span> all day.  I got dinner.  This<span class='line-break'> </span> evening I went to Marvins<span class='line-break'> </span> a whil.  Marvin went to <span class='line-break'> </span> Strait Stone to preaching.<span class='line-break'> </span> Brought me two books that<span class='line-break'> </span> I borrowed from Ethel<span class='line-break'> </span> Worsham.  I have bin reading<span class='line-break'> </span> tonight.  There is a show at<span class='line-break'> </span> Renan to night.  None of my<span class='line-break'> </span> folks did not go to see it.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben and Henry went hunting<span class='line-break'> </span> tonight.  Did not catch any thing.<span class='line-break'> </span> Professor Gambol passed<span class='line-break'> </span> here this evening on his way<span class='line-break'> </span> to Mr Edmons.  Guess he will<span class='line-break'> </span> spend the night there.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1464">
<h3><a name="page-1464">Sunday December  4, 1921</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A rainy day.  We all staid at<span class='line-break'> </span> home until after dinner.<span class='line-break'> </span> I went to Marvins late <span class='line-break'> </span> this evening.  Marvin is thinking<span class='line-break'> </span> of killing hogs in the morning.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mabel is not well yet.<span class='line-break'> </span> Hope she will be well soon.<span class='line-break'> </span> I got dinner except make a<span class='line-break'> </span> potatoe salid. Josie made that.<span class='line-break'> </span> It was fine.<span class='line-break'> </span> I and Josie have read some<span class='line-break'> </span> today in book that we<span class='line-break'> </span> borrowed.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1465">
<h3><a name="page-1465">Monday December  5, 1921</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A colde windy day.  Marvin<span class='line-break'> </span> killed hogs.  Ben &amp; Jim helped<span class='line-break'> </span> him.  They sent Reese for<span class='line-break'> </span> Martha Miller.  She come<span class='line-break'> </span> and will helpe them for<span class='line-break'> </span> several days until they<span class='line-break'> </span> move.  I was there today.  <span class='line-break'> </span> Jim and I eat dinner there.<span class='line-break'> </span> Josie got dinner at home.<span class='line-break'> </span> She made some preserves<span class='line-break'> </span> and pickel to day.  Poor<span class='line-break'> </span> little Mabel has cried the<span class='line-break'> </span> most of the day. I feel so<span class='line-break'> </span> troubled a bout her and<span class='line-break'> </span> cant do any thing to help<span class='line-break'> </span> her.<span class='line-break'> </span> The children went to<span class='line-break'> </span> school today.  It was rough<span class='line-break'> </span> on little ones.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1466">
<h3><a name="page-1466">Tuesday December  6, 1921</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Ben &amp; Jim killed<span class='line-break'> </span> their hogs, 6 in number.  They<span class='line-break'> </span> were very fat.  Marvin and<span class='line-break'> </span> Claud Edmons and a darkey<span class='line-break'> </span> Booker Callands.  Alcie Green<span class='line-break'> </span> helped me.  We got on fine<span class='line-break'> </span> I thought.  Nellie Brumfield<span class='line-break'> </span> come this morning.  Mr. Fretwell[?]<span class='line-break'> </span> brough her down.<span class='line-break'> </span> Martha Miller worked on lard<span class='line-break'> </span> for Carrie most all day.<span class='line-break'> </span> Marvin Smith &amp; Ben Brumfield<span class='line-break'> </span> went to Gretna late this<span class='line-break'> </span> evening.  They have not got<span class='line-break'> </span> home yet.<span class='line-break'> </span> I am so near a sleep I cant<span class='line-break'> </span> write much<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
<p> I have counted the times that I<span class='line-break'> </span> have bin fishing this year.  I have <span class='line-break'> </span> bin thirty nine times.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1467">
<h3><a name="page-1467">Wednesday December  7, 1921</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Ben helped<span class='line-break'> </span> Mr Edmons kill hogs.<span class='line-break'> </span> Jim helped to grind sausag<span class='line-break'> </span> and carrie the lard to the <span class='line-break'> </span> spring then shucked some<span class='line-break'> </span> corn.  This evening Jim &amp; Ben<span class='line-break'> </span> helped to load the waggons<span class='line-break'> </span> for Marvin.  They intend to<span class='line-break'> </span> move away tomorow.  I hope <span class='line-break'> </span> they may have a good day.<span class='line-break'> </span> Josie and Nellie ground sausag<span class='line-break'> </span> and seasoned it and got<span class='line-break'> </span> dinner &amp; supper.<span class='line-break'> </span> I staid at the wash house<span class='line-break'> </span> and dried up the lard.  We<span class='line-break'> </span> made a good lot of lard.<span class='line-break'> </span> The children went to school.<span class='line-break'> </span> Oh how we all will miss<span class='line-break'> </span> Marvin and all of the<span class='line-break'> </span> family.  I think it may be<span class='line-break'> </span> the best thing that he can do.<span class='line-break'> </span> Time will tell them that lives to see.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1468">
<h3><a name="page-1468">Thursday December  8, 1921</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A cloudy day.  No rain until a<span class='line-break'> </span> bout night.  Marvin moved his <span class='line-break'> </span> family to Gretna today and <span class='line-break'> </span> Norman Booker moved to the place<span class='line-break'> </span> that he moved from.  Ben went with<span class='line-break'> </span> a load.  Lee Brumfield &amp; Johnson Reynolds<span class='line-break'> </span> and Willie Mayhew all carried<span class='line-break'> </span> a load.  The family went on the car.<span class='line-break'> </span> Nellie Brumfield went with them<span class='line-break'> </span> on her way home.  William Gilbert<span class='line-break'> </span> and Reese Smith carried the cows.<span class='line-break'> </span> Alcie Callender washed here<span class='line-break'> </span> today and helped me clean<span class='line-break'> </span> the hog faces.  I cleaned the<span class='line-break'> </span> feet myself.  Virginia Harvey<span class='line-break'> </span> come today.  Josie and Virginia<span class='line-break'> </span> made some candy.  Josie fried<span class='line-break'> </span> sausag and caned some.<span class='line-break'> </span> She got dinner &amp; supper.<span class='line-break'> </span> Jim helped Norman Booker<span class='line-break'> </span> put up his range this evening.<span class='line-break'> </span> I hope they all will be pleased<span class='line-break'> </span> with the change they made.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1469">
<h3><a name="page-1469">Friday December  9, 1921</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A beautiful day.  Jim Brumfield<span class='line-break'> </span> went with Normon Booker to Mr<span class='line-break'> </span> Dave Bookers to get his cows.<span class='line-break'> </span> They got back home a bout twelve<span class='line-break'> </span> oclock.  Ben did not get home<span class='line-break'> </span> until dark.  Him and Lee Brumfield<span class='line-break'> </span> helped Marvin to fix up his things.<span class='line-break'> </span> Jim mended up the toy house<span class='line-break'> </span> that Marvins children did have.<span class='line-break'> </span> Kate Harvey come a little while.<span class='line-break'> </span> Oh how she will mis Marvins<span class='line-break'> </span> folks.  I have felt all day like<span class='line-break'> </span> something bad had happened.<span class='line-break'> </span> Josie went up to Mr Booker<span class='line-break'> </span> a few minutes this morning.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mrs Booker was very busy.<span class='line-break'> </span> I boiled meat and made<span class='line-break'> </span> scrapple today.<span class='line-break'> </span> The children went to school.<span class='line-break'> </span> Reece and Paul come with Ben <span class='line-break'> </span> home.  They will carrie a load<span class='line-break'> </span> of plunder home tomorrow if<span class='line-break'> </span> nothing happens to hinder.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1470">
<h3><a name="page-1470">Saturday December 10, 1921</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A clear colde day.  Ben &amp; Jim<span class='line-break'> </span> helped Marvins boys load on some<span class='line-break'> </span> things this morning then moved a<span class='line-break'> </span> cureing of tobacco.  Then they<span class='line-break'> </span> sawed some wood.  Finished what <span class='line-break'> </span> they had at the wood pile <span class='line-break'> </span> and moved the engine to night.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben &amp; Jim and Norman Booker<span class='line-break'> </span> went to Strait Stone.  Jim<span class='line-break'> </span> come home about nine oclock.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben and Norman has come in<span class='line-break'> </span> at eleven oclock.  Josie caned<span class='line-break'> </span> some meat this evening.  I think<span class='line-break'> </span> we brok about five cans.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mrs Booker staid with us<span class='line-break'> </span> tonight while the men was<span class='line-break'> </span> gone.  I think I will like <span class='line-break'> </span> her fine but no one can<span class='line-break'> </span> fill Carries place.  I can<span class='line-break'> </span> hardly stay at home I mis<span class='line-break'> </span> Marvins folks so much.<span class='line-break'> </span> Franklin and Edna is going to bed.<span class='line-break'> </span> 11 oclock</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1471">
<h3><a name="page-1471">Sunday December 11, 1921</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Jim &amp; Ben gave the<span class='line-break'> </span> cows some corn stalks this morning.<span class='line-break'> </span> I got a snack for dinner.  Josie<span class='line-break'> </span> dressed the children.  We eat before<span class='line-break'> </span> twelve and went to Marvins.<span class='line-break'> </span> Marvin and the three boys brought<span class='line-break'> </span> William Gilbert to Mr Bookers<span class='line-break'> </span> and then come here.  They would<span class='line-break'> </span> not eat dinner here.  I went<span class='line-break'> </span> with them home.  Ben and his <span class='line-break'> </span> folks went on Bens car.  I come<span class='line-break'> </span> with Ben back.  The children<span class='line-break'> </span> all done very well.<span class='line-break'> </span> Jim staid at home.  He done<span class='line-break'> </span> several things.  He had a good <span class='line-break'> </span> fire in the range and fire<span class='line-break'> </span> place and had brought water<span class='line-break'> </span> when we got home.  Had turned <span class='line-break'> </span> the cow to the calf.<span class='line-break'> </span> We fixed supper and all eat.<span class='line-break'> </span> I am so glad that I got to see<span class='line-break'> </span> Carrie.  She seems to be satisfied.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1472">
<h3><a name="page-1472">Monday December 12, 1921</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Jim &amp; Ben shucked<span class='line-break'> </span> a shock of corn and gave the<span class='line-break'> </span> stalk to the cows.  Then they loaded<span class='line-break'> </span> up the car with Jims scrap meat<span class='line-break'> </span> and sausage, a few chickens and<span class='line-break'> </span> went to Chatham.  I think they<span class='line-break'> </span> did fine.  They attended to several<span class='line-break'> </span> things and got home before dark.<span class='line-break'> </span> I am very glad that they went.<span class='line-break'> </span> The roads are very good now.<span class='line-break'> </span> Josie scrubed some floors and<span class='line-break'> </span> got dinner.  I went to George<span class='line-break'> </span> Blairs.  Denia was not at home.<span class='line-break'> </span> She had gone to Altavista with<span class='line-break'> </span> Otho and Sallie.  I would of bin<span class='line-break'> </span> glad to see her but I dont<span class='line-break'> </span> blame her.  If it was me I think [?]<span class='line-break'> </span> go evry chance I could get.<span class='line-break'> </span> I spent a pleasant evening<span class='line-break'> </span> with the girls.  The children<span class='line-break'> </span> went to school today.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1473">
<h3><a name="page-1473">Tuesday December 13, 1921</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A cool windy day.  Jim &amp; Ben<span class='line-break'> </span> shucked some corn.  The wind<span class='line-break'> </span> blowed so that they could hardly<span class='line-break'> </span> shuck.  I boiled some hogs<span class='line-break'> </span> ears for dinner.  Josie made<span class='line-break'> </span> bread &amp; coffee.  I put feathers <span class='line-break'> </span> in Josies new bed tick this<span class='line-break'> </span> morning.  This evening I went<span class='line-break'> </span> to the store and bought a few<span class='line-break'> </span> things.  I walked up there <span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; back.  I brought back 7<span class='line-break'> </span> pounds 6 of coffee &amp; one of soda.<span class='line-break'> </span> I went to see Kate Harvey<span class='line-break'> </span> a few minutes.  She was busy<span class='line-break'> </span> fixing up after hog killing.<span class='line-break'> </span> I come by Mollies.  They<span class='line-break'> </span> were very busy abought<span class='line-break'> </span> their land &amp; sausage.  I did<span class='line-break'> </span> not stay to bother them long.<span class='line-break'> </span> I have bin working on a quilt.<span class='line-break'> </span> Tonight little Mabel is up yet. <span class='line-break'> </span> I hear her talking.<span class='line-break'> </span> 8:30 oclock</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1474">
<h3><a name="page-1474">Wednesday December 14, 1921</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A windy day.  Very disagreeable.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben and Ben hauled some leaves<span class='line-break'> </span> and put in the stable.<span class='line-break'> </span> Alcie Callands washed here<span class='line-break'> </span> today.  The clothes most blowed<span class='line-break'> </span> a way.  I got them this evening.<span class='line-break'> </span> I have staid at home all day to<span class='line-break'> </span> day.  We had turnip salid<span class='line-break'> </span> for dinner and sweet potatoes.<span class='line-break'> </span> Tonight there is two men<span class='line-break'> </span> here say they are Mormon<span class='line-break'> </span> preachers.  We dreaded them<span class='line-break'> </span> but they are very pleasant.<span class='line-break'> </span> The children went to school.<span class='line-break'> </span> Josie commenced to change<span class='line-break'> </span> her dress this evening.  I<span class='line-break'> </span> comenced to make some <span class='line-break'> </span> sheets.  Tonight I have read.<span class='line-break'> </span> Did not try to work any.<span class='line-break'> </span> It is now nearly ten oclock<span class='line-break'> </span> and I must go bed.<span class='line-break'> </span> Oh how I miss Carrie.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1475">
<h3><a name="page-1475">Thursday December 15, 1921</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A beautiful day.  Ben went<span class='line-break'> </span> to Mr Edmons's to saw wood.<span class='line-break'> </span> Was there all day.  Jim shucked<span class='line-break'> </span> corn.  The Mormon preachers<span class='line-break'> </span> went a way early this morning.<span class='line-break'> </span> I am not sorry that they<span class='line-break'> </span> staid here last night.  Josie ironed<span class='line-break'> </span> all the morning.  I got dinner.<span class='line-break'> </span> This evening I went to Mr<span class='line-break'> </span> Bookers.  Sallie &amp; Isla Blair<span class='line-break'> </span> was there.  Evry thing looked<span class='line-break'> </span> very nice up there but oh<span class='line-break'> </span> how I mis Marvin &amp; Carrie.<span class='line-break'> </span> No one knows but my self.<span class='line-break'> </span> I have peiced on a quilt some<span class='line-break'> </span> tonight.  Mabel has tried<span class='line-break'> </span> her self tonight and tried<span class='line-break'> </span> Josie.  I am sorry for them<span class='line-break'> </span> both and cant them.<span class='line-break'> </span> Jim has a bad cough.  I<span class='line-break'> </span> wish he could get well<span class='line-break'> </span> of it.  The children went to school to day.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1476">
<h3><a name="page-1476">Friday December 16, 1921</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A partly day.  Jim &amp; Ben<span class='line-break'> </span> hauled up some corn <span class='line-break'> </span> stalks this morning.  This<span class='line-break'> </span> evening they cut wood for <span class='line-break'> </span> Norman Booker.  Tonight Ben<span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; Josie went to Strait<span class='line-break'> </span> Stone.  Did not stay long.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mabel staid up until<span class='line-break'> </span> they come home.<span class='line-break'> </span> Marvin Smith come today.<span class='line-break'> </span> He eat dinner with us.<span class='line-break'> </span> Josie ironed most allday.  I <span class='line-break'> </span> got dinner except make the<span class='line-break'> </span> biskit.  Josie done that.  I stewed<span class='line-break'> </span> pumpkin the most of the day.<span class='line-break'> </span> Lizzie Bennett and Lee Brumfield<span class='line-break'> </span> gave me a pumpkin.  We did<span class='line-break'> </span> not make one this year.<span class='line-break'> </span> Eleck Gilbert hauled and <span class='line-break'> </span> put wood under shelter<span class='line-break'> </span> to day.  I am glad of it.<span class='line-break'> </span> The children went to school.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1477">
<h3><a name="page-1477">Saturday December 17, 1921</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A cloudy day.  No rain until<span class='line-break'> </span> tonight.  Jim &amp; Ben hauled some<span class='line-break'> </span> stalks this morning and cut<span class='line-break'> </span> them this evening.  Mr Booker<span class='line-break'> </span> helped them to cut them.<span class='line-break'> </span> Josie got dinner &amp; supper.<span class='line-break'> </span> She went to Reynols and<span class='line-break'> </span> got a nice bucket of salit<span class='line-break'> </span> for tomorrows dinner.  We<span class='line-break'> </span> hope that Carrie Smith and<span class='line-break'> </span> the children will come.<span class='line-break'> </span> Jim made a pen this evening<span class='line-break'> </span> and got up the turkeys.<span class='line-break'> </span> He put four up in the<span class='line-break'> </span> hog pen to keep a few <span class='line-break'> </span> days.  They smell of wilde<span class='line-break'> </span> onions so bad.<span class='line-break'> </span> I spent most of the day<span class='line-break'> </span> mending up some clothes.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben mended Henrys shoes<span class='line-break'> </span> this evening.  I guess there<span class='line-break'> </span> will be lots of mending done<span class='line-break'> </span> this winter &amp; spring.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1478">
<h3><a name="page-1478">Sunday December 18, 1921</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A clear cool day.  We all<span class='line-break'> </span> staid at home all day.<span class='line-break'> </span> Carrie and all the children<span class='line-break'> </span> come and spent the day.<span class='line-break'> </span> Reese was driving the car.<span class='line-break'> </span> I hope they got home ok.<span class='line-break'> </span> I cant help being uneasy a<span class='line-break'> </span> bout them.  There is so many<span class='line-break'> </span> things that can happen.<span class='line-break'> </span> Kate Harvey come and eat<span class='line-break'> </span> dinner with us.  I was so<span class='line-break'> </span> glad that they all come.<span class='line-break'> </span> Would of bin glad that<span class='line-break'> </span> Marvin could of come two.<span class='line-break'> </span> Josie and Martha Miller<span class='line-break'> </span> got dinner.  Martha<span class='line-break'> </span> Miller come with Carrie.<span class='line-break'> </span> She is going to help<span class='line-break'> </span> Mollie Reynols tomorrow.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1479">
<h3><a name="page-1479">Monday December 19, 1921</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Jim and Ben<span class='line-break'> </span> shucked some corn and<span class='line-break'> </span> hauled stalks and put in<span class='line-break'> </span> the stable.  Josie washed dishes<span class='line-break'> </span> and milked the cows.  I went<span class='line-break'> </span> to Chatham with Johson &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span> Mollie Reynols.  Clack Hubbard<span class='line-break'> </span> and Christenia Reynols went<span class='line-break'> </span> with them also.  I dont think<span class='line-break'> </span> any body bought much.<span class='line-break'> </span> They ask such prices for what they<span class='line-break'> </span> had to sell.  Henry &amp; Edna<span class='line-break'> </span> went to school.  Franklin is not<span class='line-break'> </span> well.  Virginia Harvey come<span class='line-break'> </span> here and Josie and Virginia made<span class='line-break'> </span> candy for to treat the school<span class='line-break'> </span> children on Wednesday.<span class='line-break'> </span> I had a good day.  I met with<span class='line-break'> </span> several of my kind folks and<span class='line-break'> </span> acquaintances.  I was so glad to<span class='line-break'> </span> go and every thing [?] of good.<span class='line-break'> </span> Alice Thomson was at Chatham.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1480">
<h3><a name="page-1480">Tuesday December 20, 1921</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Ben sawed wood<span class='line-break'> </span> at Reynols.  Jim hauled chaff<span class='line-break'> </span> and put it on the land.  Norman<span class='line-break'> </span> Booker had the horse Jake a while<span class='line-break'> </span> this morning.  Henry &amp; Edna went <span class='line-break'> </span> to school.  Josie has bin cleaning<span class='line-break'> </span> up the house and yard all day.<span class='line-break'> </span> I got dinner and washed<span class='line-break'> </span> the dishes while Josie cracked<span class='line-break'> </span> and picked walnuts for a cake.<span class='line-break'> </span> I got a letter from Effie<span class='line-break'> </span> Brumfield.  Also a year book<span class='line-break'> </span> from the family, a nice one.<span class='line-break'> </span> I am glad of it.<span class='line-break'> </span> Hope I may live to write it <span class='line-break'> </span> out.  I feel that I am in the<span class='line-break'> </span> way now.  I am olde fashioned<span class='line-break'> </span> and slow to get about.<span class='line-break'> </span> All of the young ones that live<span class='line-break'> </span> to be olde will know how I feel.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1481">
<h3><a name="page-1481">Wednesday December 21, 1921</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Jim hauled some<span class='line-break'> </span> chaff this morning.  This evening<span class='line-break'> </span> he shucked corn.  Ben worked<span class='line-break'> </span> on the dineing room floor this<span class='line-break'> </span> morning.  This evening he went<span class='line-break'> </span> to Strait Stone.  I went with<span class='line-break'> </span> him.  Kate Harvey come this<span class='line-break'> </span> morning.  Kate and I dressed<span class='line-break'> </span> 4 turkeys.  One for Jim, one<span class='line-break'> </span> for Marvin, one for Josie, and<span class='line-break'> </span> one for Kate.  This evening<span class='line-break'> </span> Marvin come and got his turkey <span class='line-break'> </span> and ham boiler.  He had Hazel &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span> Eva with him.  I went with him<span class='line-break'> </span> as far as Reynols mail box and<span class='line-break'> </span> walked home.  Mollie Reynols<span class='line-break'> </span> was not at home.<span class='line-break'> </span> Hattie Gilbert washed here today.<span class='line-break'> </span> The wind is blowing to night.  I<span class='line-break'> </span> reckon they will all blow of the<span class='line-break'> </span> line.  Heard today that Mrs Jessie<span class='line-break'> </span> Hutcherson has a son.  There is a lot<span class='line-break'> </span> of travlins done today.  The school closed today for holiday.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben[?] has gone to the school house to night.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1482">
<h3><a name="page-1482">Thursday December 22, 1921</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A colde day partly cloudy.<span class='line-break'> </span> Hailing and snowing tonight.<span class='line-break'> </span> Jim shucked some corn and<span class='line-break'> </span> toated stalks for the cows.  Ben<span class='line-break'> </span> sawed wood at Kate Harveys.<span class='line-break'> </span> Brought the engine &amp; saw home<span class='line-break'> </span> tonight.  Ben went to Strait Stone<span class='line-break'> </span> tonight.  He went for medicine<span class='line-break'> </span> for Mabel.  She has a colde<span class='line-break'> </span> and is very hoarse.  We are a<span class='line-break'> </span> fraid she will have the croup.<span class='line-break'> </span> Josie ironed today and worked on<span class='line-break'> </span> her cakes some.  I got dinner.<span class='line-break'> </span> Denia Blair come a little while.<span class='line-break'> </span> I was glad that she come.  Two <span class='line-break'> </span> of the Doss girls come a few<span class='line-break'> </span> minutes.  They borrowed a last.<span class='line-break'> </span> Said they wanted to mend shoes.<span class='line-break'> </span> I am sorry that it is weathering.<span class='line-break'> </span> Did hope it would stay good<span class='line-break'> </span> until Jim could get home.<span class='line-break'> </span> We sent Kates turkey to her this morning.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1483">
<h3><a name="page-1483">Friday December 23, 1921</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  The land was<span class='line-break'> </span> covered with hail and snow but<span class='line-break'> </span> it nearly all melted before night.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben &amp; Jim did not do much of <span class='line-break'> </span> anything this morning.  This evening<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben carried Jim to Gretna on his<span class='line-break'> </span> way to Chatham to spend the<span class='line-break'> </span> holidays with his folks.  Josie and<span class='line-break'> </span> Henry went with them.  They got home<span class='line-break'> </span> in good time.  They bought several<span class='line-break'> </span> things.  Among them they got some cow<span class='line-break'> </span> feed.  I am so glad of that.  Ben is<span class='line-break'> </span> in the basement not trying to stain<span class='line-break'> </span> the floors.  Josie made me a nice<span class='line-break'> </span> apron tonight.  I am glad of it.  I got<span class='line-break'> </span> several Xmas cards from the<span class='line-break'> </span> grand children &amp; friends.  I killed<span class='line-break'> </span> 4 chickens and dressed them ready<span class='line-break'> </span> to cook.  Two for Jim.  Heard to<span class='line-break'> </span> day that Oscar Brumfield is sick.<span class='line-break'> </span> Hope he may soon be well.  I do hope<span class='line-break'> </span> that Mabel will soon be well<span class='line-break'> </span> a gain.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1484">
<h3><a name="page-1484">Saturday December 24, 1921</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A cloudy day.  Rain tonight.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben went to William Gilberts<span class='line-break'> </span> this morning and carried some<span class='line-break'> </span> things for them that Carrie sent<span class='line-break'> </span> and Josie sent some things two<span class='line-break'> </span> for their children.  Henry &amp; Ben<span class='line-break'> </span> hunted some this evening.  Did not<span class='line-break'> </span> get any game.  We boiled some<span class='line-break'> </span> ham.  I boiled the last of the <span class='line-break'> </span> hogs feet.  Josie baked a cake.<span class='line-break'> </span> She ironed all the morning.<span class='line-break'> </span> Irvin Harvey come this morning<span class='line-break'> </span> and got their cow &amp; little calf.<span class='line-break'> </span> The children has bad colds.<span class='line-break'> </span> They cant hardly wait for <span class='line-break'> </span> Santy to come.  They are a<span class='line-break'> </span> sleep now all but Henry.<span class='line-break'> </span> I guess he is a wake.<span class='line-break'> </span> Well I am glad that Xmas is<span class='line-break'> </span> here.  Hope nothing bad will happen.<span class='line-break'> </span> I got a nice box of candy from<span class='line-break'> </span> BlacksBurg today &amp; a letter from John<span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; a card from Julia Fergerson.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1485">
<h3><a name="page-1485">Sunday December 25, 1921</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A rainy day.  Not very colde.<span class='line-break'> </span> We all staid at home all<span class='line-break'> </span> day.  Irvin Harvey come a <span class='line-break'> </span> few minutes this morning.<span class='line-break'> </span> He brought me a dress<span class='line-break'> </span> that his mother had made<span class='line-break'> </span> for me, a Christmas gift.<span class='line-break'> </span> The children have a good<span class='line-break'> </span> time today with their toys<span class='line-break'> </span> and dolls.  I hope they may<span class='line-break'> </span> not have the croup tonight.<span class='line-break'> </span> There has bin very little <span class='line-break'> </span> passing of people today.  The<span class='line-break'> </span> roads are bad.<span class='line-break'> </span> I have bin thinkin of all of<span class='line-break'> </span> the children.  Wish I could<span class='line-break'> </span> see all of them.  I mis Carrie<span class='line-break'> </span> and her folks so much.  If the<span class='line-break'> </span> weather stays bad I wont<span class='line-break'> </span> see them in some time.<span class='line-break'> </span> Well I may never see another<span class='line-break'> </span> Xmas.  I am not feeling well now.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1486">
<h3><a name="page-1486">Monday December 26, 1921</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A cloudy day.  No weather yet.<span class='line-break'> </span> We all staid at home until<span class='line-break'> </span> noon.  This evening Ben &amp; family <span class='line-break'> </span> went to Jim Powers.  Mrs Car<span class='line-break'> </span> had a Xmas tree for her<span class='line-break'> </span> grand children.  She had lots<span class='line-break'> </span> of presents for her children<span class='line-break'> </span> and grand children.  She<span class='line-break'> </span> sent me a nice hand pocket.<span class='line-break'> </span> I am glad of it.  I did not<span class='line-break'> </span> go.  Some one had to attend to<span class='line-break'> </span> the cows.  I done that.  Brought<span class='line-break'> </span> water and wood for in the <span class='line-break'> </span> morning.  No one has bin to see<span class='line-break'> </span> us yet.  The roads is bad.  I hope<span class='line-break'> </span> some one will come soon.<span class='line-break'> </span> I want to go to see Carrie<span class='line-break'> </span> but cant whil the roads is<span class='line-break'> </span> so bad.  Mabel is so carried<span class='line-break'> </span> a way over her doll she<span class='line-break'> </span> cant go to sleep.<span class='line-break'> </span> 9 oclock</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1487">
<h3><a name="page-1487">Tuesday December 27, 1921</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Ben &amp; family <span class='line-break'> </span> staid at home the most <span class='line-break'> </span> of the day.  Miss Willie<span class='line-break'> </span> Wooding &amp; Virginia Wooding<span class='line-break'> </span> come a while this morning.<span class='line-break'> </span> I did not see them.  I would<span class='line-break'> </span> of liked to of bin at home.<span class='line-break'> </span> I went to George Blairs<span class='line-break'> </span> this morning.  Mr Norman Booker<span class='line-break'> </span> carried me a part of the<span class='line-break'> </span> way.  Georges folks had company.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mr &amp; Mrs Anderson was there.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ren Worsham &amp; family, Ernest<span class='line-break'> </span> Craddock and family, Nettie<span class='line-break'> </span> Hendricks and baby, Otho &amp; Sallie.<span class='line-break'> </span> They had very good dinner.<span class='line-break'> </span> Plenty of everything that they needed.<span class='line-break'> </span> I think all enjoyed them selves.<span class='line-break'> </span> George Jr[?] brought me home.<span class='line-break'> </span> I was glad.  I did so much<span class='line-break'> </span> want to see some of Marvins<span class='line-break'> </span> folks today.  Ethel Worsham gave me<span class='line-break'> </span> a pair of gloves for a Xmas gift.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1488">
<h3><a name="page-1488">Wednesday December 28, 1921</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Ben &amp; Josie staid<span class='line-break'> </span> at home until after dinner<span class='line-break'> </span> then they went to Mr Bookers<span class='line-break'> </span> a while.  The Bookers had a lot<span class='line-break'> </span> of company.  Tonight Ben carried<span class='line-break'> </span> his family and to Reynols.  We<span class='line-break'> </span> have just got home after ten<span class='line-break'> </span> oclock.<span class='line-break'> </span> I went to Reynols today and<span class='line-break'> </span> eat dinner.  Alice Thomson<span class='line-break'> </span> and family and Clack Hubbard<span class='line-break'> </span> and family was there.  The men<span class='line-break'> </span> folks went hunting.  They killed<span class='line-break'> </span> several birds.  Mollie had a<span class='line-break'> </span> very nice dinner and I did enjoy it.<span class='line-break'> </span> We all got cards from Carrie<span class='line-break'> </span> today.  I want to see them all<span class='line-break'> </span> so much but cant go unless<span class='line-break'> </span> some one would take me.<span class='line-break'> </span> Reubin Reynols brought me home<span class='line-break'> </span> this evening.  Cliften went away<span class='line-break'> </span> this morning.  I wish them all well.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1489">
<h3><a name="page-1489">Thursday December 29, 1921</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A clear colde day.  We all<span class='line-break'> </span> staid at home today.  Lee &amp; Hugh<span class='line-break'> </span> Brumfield eat dinner with us.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben &amp; Lee hunted rabbits.<span class='line-break'> </span> They killed several.<span class='line-break'> </span> Josie ironed some tonight.<span class='line-break'> </span> I am disapointed.  I was<span class='line-break'> </span> in hopes to get to see<span class='line-break'> </span> Carrie this Xmas but now <span class='line-break'> </span> I dont expect I will.  It <span class='line-break'> </span> has got so colde.<span class='line-break'> </span> Hugh Brumfield is spending<span class='line-break'> </span> the night with Henry.<span class='line-break'> </span> I have bin reading to night.<span class='line-break'> </span> nearly eleven oclock</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1490">
<h3><a name="page-1490">Friday December 30, 1921</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A colde clear day.  We had<span class='line-break'> </span> company all day and until<span class='line-break'> </span> bed time.  Henry Brumfield &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span> Irvin Harvey, Floyed Reynols, Aubra<span class='line-break'> </span> Brumfield, Hugh Brumfield &amp; <span class='line-break'> </span> his mother &amp; Bulah &amp; Else<span class='line-break'> </span> was here at dinner and Mollie<span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; Rubin &amp; Robbert Floid<span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; Chritenia Reynols was here<span class='line-break'> </span> tonight.  I was glad to<span class='line-break'> </span> have them all to see us.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1491">
<h3><a name="page-1491">Saturday December 31, 1921</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>Some clouds and a colde<span class='line-break'> </span> south wind.  Ben &amp; family exct<span class='line-break'> </span> Henry and I went to Marvins.<span class='line-break'> </span> We met Carrie &amp; the children<span class='line-break'> </span> comeing here.  They went home<span class='line-break'> </span> and we all had dinner<span class='line-break'> </span> with them.  John Brumfield<span class='line-break'> </span> come to Marvins a while.  He<span class='line-break'> </span> had bin to dinner.<span class='line-break'> </span> Carrie &amp; all of the children<span class='line-break'> </span> come home with us.  I am<span class='line-break'> </span> glad to have them.  Marvin staid<span class='line-break'> </span> at home to take care of things.<span class='line-break'> </span> Henry went home with<span class='line-break'> </span> Hugh last evening to spend<span class='line-break'> </span> the evening and night.  He is<span class='line-break'> </span> at home to night.  I am anxious<span class='line-break'> </span> for Jim to come back as he<span class='line-break'> </span> intends to.  I am glad that we<span class='line-break'> </span> are all well and all of my folks<span class='line-break'> </span> are reasonably well as for as I<span class='line-break'> </span> know except Lonnie Bennett</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1492">
<h3><a name="page-1492">Memoranda (i)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>and he is improving I hope.<span class='line-break'> </span> I had a letter from Julia<span class='line-break'> </span> Fergerson.  She sent me a nice<span class='line-break'> </span> handkerchief.  Carrie gave me<span class='line-break'> </span> a box of stationary &amp; Reese<span class='line-break'> </span> gave me a box of nice candy.<span class='line-break'> </span> Well so ends this year.<span class='line-break'> </span> It has not bin so good but<span class='line-break'> </span> I would be glad to that<span class='line-break'> </span> the next wont be any worse.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ten oclock Sat night 1921</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1493">
<h3><a name="page-1493">Memoranda (ii)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>The first snow of the winter<span class='line-break'> </span> of 1921 and 1922 fell on the <span class='line-break'> </span> 22nd of December 1921.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1494">
<h3><a name="page-1494">Memoranda (iii)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>I owe Ben four dollars<span class='line-break'> </span> and thirty cts this the 8th<span class='line-break'> </span> of November 1921<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
<p> [Entry is crossed out.]<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
<p> [printed at the bottom of the page]<span class='line-break'> </span> Found the spotted heifer<span class='line-break'> </span> calf the 12 of April 1921</p>
</div>
</div>
